codecs="vp9, opus"'/><source data-bandwidth="124536" data-framerate="30" data-height="160" data-shorttitle="WebM 160P" data-title="Low bandwidth WebM (160P)" data-transcodekey="160p.webm" data-width="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/9a/North_Pole_Sea_Ice_1990-1999.ogv/North_Pole_Sea_Ice_1990-1999.ogv.160p.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp8, vorbis"'/><source data-bandwidth="186344" data-framerate="30" data-height="180" data-shorttitle="VP9 180P" data-title="Low bandwidth VP9 (180P)" data-transcodekey="180p.vp9.webm" data-width="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/9a/North_Pole_Sea_Ice_1990-1999.ogv/North_Pole_Sea_Ice_1990-1999.ogv.180p.vp9.webm" type='video/webm; codecs="vp9, opus"'/></video> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:North_Pole_Sea_Ice_1990-1999.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Changes in ice between 1990 and 1999</div></div></div>
<p>The Arctic Ocean is contained in a <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">polar climate</a> characterized by persistent cold and relatively narrow annual temperature ranges. Winters are characterized by the <a href="/wiki/Polar_night" title="Polar night">polar night</a>, extreme cold, frequent low-level temperature inversions, and stable weather conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cyclone" title="Cyclone">Cyclones</a> are only common on the Atlantic side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-52">[52]</a></sup> Summers are characterized by continuous <a href="/wiki/Daylight" title="Daylight">daylight</a> (<a href="/wiki/Midnight_sun" title="Midnight sun">midnight sun</a>), and air temperatures can rise slightly above 0 °C (32 °F). Cyclones are more frequent in summer and may bring rain or snow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-52">[52]</a></sup> It is cloudy year-round, with mean cloud cover ranging from 60% in winter to over 80% in summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>The temperature of the surface water of the Arctic Ocean is fairly constant at approximately −1.8 °C (28.8 °F), near the <a href="/wiki/Melting_point" title="Melting point">freezing point</a> of <a href="/wiki/Seawater" title="Seawater">seawater</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Density" title="Density">density</a> of sea water, in contrast to fresh water, increases as it nears the freezing point and thus it tends to sink. It is generally necessary that the upper 100–150 m (330–490 ft) of ocean water cools to the freezing point for sea ice to form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> In the winter, the relatively warm ocean water exerts a moderating influence, even when covered by ice. This is one reason why the Arctic does not experience the extreme temperatures seen on the <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctic continent</a>.
</p><p>There is considerable seasonal variation in how much pack ice of the Arctic ice pack covers the Arctic Ocean. Much of the Arctic ice pack is also covered in snow for about 10 months of the year. The maximum snow cover is in March or April—about 20–50 cm (7.9–19.7 in) over the frozen ocean.
</p><p>The climate of the Arctic region has varied significantly during the Earth's history. During the <a href="/wiki/Paleocene%E2%80%93Eocene_Thermal_Maximum" title="Paleocene–Eocene Thermal Maximum">Paleocene–Eocene Thermal Maximum</a> 55 million years ago, when the global climate underwent a warming of approximately 5–8 °C (9–14 °F), the region reached an average annual temperature of 10–20 °C (50–68 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shellito2003_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shellito2003-57">[57]</a></sup> The surface waters of the northernmost<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Arctic Ocean warmed, seasonally at least, enough to support tropical lifeforms (the <a href="/wiki/Dinoflagellate" title="Dinoflagellate">dinoflagellates</a> <i>Apectodinium augustum</i>) requiring surface temperatures of over 22 °C (72 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sluijs2006_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sluijs2006-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>Currently, the Arctic region is warming twice as fast as the rest of the planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biology">Biology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arctic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Biology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1575" data-file-width="2100" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg/220px-Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg/330px-Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg/440px-Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Polar_bears_near_north_pole.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Three <a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">polar bears</a> approach <a href="/wiki/USS_Honolulu_(SSN-718)" title="USS Honolulu (SSN-718)">USS <i>Honolulu</i></a> near the <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">North Pole</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Due to the pronounced seasonality of 2–6 months of <a href="/wiki/Midnight_sun" title="Midnight sun">midnight sun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polar_night" title="Polar night">polar night</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> in the Arctic Ocean, the <a href="/wiki/Primary_production" title="Primary production">primary production</a> of photosynthesizing organisms such as <a href="/wiki/Ice_algae" title="Ice algae">ice algae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phytoplankton" title="Phytoplankton">phytoplankton</a> is limited to the spring and summer months (March/April to September).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Important consumers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_producers" title="Primary producers">primary producers</a> in the central Arctic Ocean and the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">shelf seas</a> include <a href="/wiki/Zooplankton" title="Zooplankton">zooplankton</a>, especially <a href="/wiki/Copepod" title="Copepod">copepods</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Calanus_finmarchicus" title="Calanus finmarchicus">Calanus finmarchicus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Calanus_glacialis" title="Calanus glacialis">Calanus glacialis</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Calanus_hyperboreus" title="Calanus hyperboreus">Calanus hyperboreus</a></i>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[64]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Krill" title="Krill">euphausiids</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-65">[65]</a></sup> as well as ice-associated <a href="/wiki/Fauna" title="Fauna">fauna</a> (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Amphipoda" title="Amphipoda">amphipods</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-64">[64]</a></sup> These <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_consumers" title="Primary consumers">primary consumers</a> form an important link between the primary producers and higher <a href="/wiki/Trophic_level" title="Trophic level">trophic levels</a>. The composition of higher trophic levels in the Arctic Ocean varies with region (Atlantic side vs. Pacific side) and with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea-ice" title="Sea-ice">sea-ice</a> cover. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secondary_consumer" title="Secondary consumer">Secondary consumers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Barents_Sea" title="Barents Sea">Barents Sea</a>, an Atlantic-influenced Arctic shelf sea, are mainly sub-Arctic species including <a href="/wiki/Herring" title="Herring">herring</a>, young <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_cod" title="Atlantic cod">cod</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Capelin" title="Capelin">capelin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-65">[65]</a></sup> In ice-covered regions of the central Arctic Ocean, <a href="/wiki/Boreogadus_saida" title="Boreogadus saida">polar cod</a> is a central predator of primary consumers. The <a href="/wiki/Apex_predator" title="Apex predator">apex predators</a> in the Arctic Ocean—<a href="/wiki/Marine_mammal" title="Marine mammal">marine mammals</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">seals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whales</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">polar bears</a>—prey upon fish.
</p><p>Endangered marine species in the Arctic Ocean include <a href="/wiki/Walrus" title="Walrus">walruses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whales</a>. The area has a fragile <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a>, and it is especially exposed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">climate change</a>, because it warms faster than the rest of the world. <a href="/wiki/Lion%27s_mane_jellyfish" title="Lion's mane jellyfish">Lion's mane jellyfish</a> are abundant in the waters of the Arctic, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banded_gunnel" title="Banded gunnel">banded gunnel</a> is the only species of <a href="/wiki/Pholidae" title="Pholidae">gunnel</a> that lives in the ocean.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Minke_Whale_(NOAA).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="321" data-file-width="532" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Minke_Whale_%28NOAA%29.jpg/220px-Minke_Whale_%28NOAA%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Minke_Whale_%28NOAA%29.jpg/330px-Minke_Whale_%28NOAA%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Minke_Whale_%28NOAA%29.jpg/440px-Minke_Whale_%28NOAA%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Minke_Whale_(NOAA).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">Minke whale</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Walruses_on_ice_floes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Walruses_on_ice_floes.jpg/220px-Walruses_on_ice_floes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Walruses_on_ice_floes.jpg/330px-Walruses_on_ice_floes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Walruses_on_ice_floes.jpg/440px-Walruses_on_ice_floes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Walruses_on_ice_floes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Walruses on Arctic ice floe</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arctic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Natural resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Natural_resources_of_the_Arctic" title="Natural resources of the Arctic">Natural resources of the Arctic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Territorial_claims_in_the_Arctic" title="Territorial claims in the Arctic">Territorial claims in the Arctic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marine_mammal" title="Marine mammal">Marine mammal</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Petroleum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_gas_field" title="Natural gas field">fields</a>, <a href="/wiki/Placer_deposit" title="Placer deposit">placer deposits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manganese_nodule" title="Manganese nodule">polymetallic nodules</a>, sand and gravel <a href="/wiki/Construction_aggregate" title="Construction aggregate">aggregates</a>, fish, seals and whales can all be found in abundance in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buixade_Farre_2014_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-Buixade_Farre_2014-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>The political dead zone near the centre of the sea is also the focus of a mounting dispute between the United States, Russia, Canada, Norway, and Denmark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> It is significant for the global <a href="/wiki/Energy_market" title="Energy market">energy market</a> because it may hold 25% or more of the world's undiscovered oil and gas resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_concerns">Environmental concerns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arctic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Environmental concerns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Arctic" title="Climate change in the Arctic">Climate change in the Arctic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ozone_depletion" title="Ozone depletion">Ozone depletion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pollution_in_the_Arctic_Ocean" title="Pollution in the Arctic Ocean">Pollution in the Arctic Ocean</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arctic_ice_melting">Arctic ice melting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arctic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Arctic ice melting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Arctic_ice_pack" title="Arctic ice pack">Arctic ice pack</a> is thinning, and a seasonal hole in the <a href="/wiki/Ozone_layer" title="Ozone layer">ozone layer</a> frequently occurs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Reduction of the area of Arctic sea ice reduces the planet's average <a href="/wiki/Albedo" title="Albedo">albedo</a>, possibly resulting in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> in a positive feedback mechanism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buixade_Farre_2014_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-Buixade_Farre_2014-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-R.Black_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-R.Black-69">[69]</a></sup> Research shows that the Arctic may become ice-free in the summer for the first time in human history by 2040.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nsidc2011_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-nsidc2011-71">[71]</a></sup> Estimates vary for when the last time the Arctic was ice-free: 65 million years ago when fossils indicate that plants existed there to as recently as 5,500 years ago; ice and ocean cores going back 8,000 years to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocene_thermal_maximum" title="Holocene thermal maximum">last warm period</a> or 125,000 during the <a href="/wiki/Eemian" title="Eemian">last intraglacial period</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nsidc_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nsidc-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>Warming temperatures in the Arctic may cause large amounts of fresh <a href="/wiki/Meltwater" title="Meltwater">melt-water</a> to enter the north Atlantic, possibly disrupting global <a href="/wiki/Thermohaline_circulation" title="Thermohaline circulation">ocean current patterns</a>. Potentially severe changes in the Earth's <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> might then ensue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-R.Black_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-R.Black-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p><p>As the extent of sea ice diminishes and sea level rises, the effect of storms such as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Arctic_Cyclone_of_2012" title="Great Arctic Cyclone of 2012">Great Arctic Cyclone of 2012</a> on open water increases, as does possible salt-water damage to vegetation on shore at locations such as the Mackenzie <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">Delta</a> as stronger <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">storm surges</a> become more likely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CC03513_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-CC03513-73">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">Global warming</a> has increased encounters between <a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">polar bears</a> and humans. Reduced sea ice due to melting is causing polar bears to search for new sources of food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Beginning in December 2018 and coming to an apex in February 2019, <a href="/wiki/2019_mass_invasion_of_Russian_polar_bears" title="2019 mass invasion of Russian polar bears">a mass invasion of polar bears</a> into the archipelago of <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a> caused local authorities to declare a state of emergency. Dozens of polar bears were seen entering homes, public buildings and inhabited areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A3_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-A3-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A4_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-A4-76">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clathrate_breakdown">Clathrate breakdown</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arctic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Clathrate breakdown">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Clathrate_gun_hypothesis" title="Clathrate gun hypothesis">Clathrate gun hypothesis</a></div>

<div id="annotation_30x10" style="position:absolute; left:30px; top:10px; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;">Marine extinction intensity during the <a href="/wiki/Phanerozoic" title="Phanerozoic">Phanerozoic</a></span></div>
<div id="annotation_10x15" style="position:absolute; left:10px; top:15px; font-weight:normal; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1038841319">.mw-parser-output .tooltip-dotted{border-bottom:1px dotted;cursor:help}</style><span class="rt-commentedText tooltip tooltip-dotted" title="apparent percentage of readily fossilized marine genera becoming extinct">%</span></span></div>
<div id="annotation_115x235" style="position:absolute; left:115px; top:235px; font-weight:normal; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;">Millions of years ago</span></div>
<div id="annotation_312x135" style="position:absolute; left:312px; top:135px; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/Holocene_extinction" title="Holocene extinction"><small>(H)</small></a></span></div>
<div id="annotation_275x105" style="position:absolute; left:275px; top:105px; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/Cretaceous%E2%80%93Paleogene_extinction_event" title="Cretaceous–Paleogene extinction event">K–Pg</a></span></div>
<div id="annotation_203x110" style="position:absolute; left:203px; top:110px; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/Triassic%E2%80%93Jurassic_extinction_event" title="Triassic–Jurassic extinction event">Tr–J</a></span></div>
<div id="annotation_175x50" style="position:absolute; left:175px; top:50px; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/Permian%E2%80%93Triassic_extinction_event" title="Permian–Triassic extinction event">P–Tr</a></span></div>
<div id="annotation_158x96" style="position:absolute; left:158px; top:96px; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/Capitanian_mass_extinction_event" title="Capitanian mass extinction event">Cap</a></span></div>
<div id="annotation_97x130" style="position:absolute; left:97px; top:130px; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/Late_Devonian_extinction" title="Late Devonian extinction">Late D</a></span></div>
<div id="annotation_70x110" style="position:absolute; left:70px; top:110px; line-height:110%;"><span style="background-color:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/Late_Ordovician_mass_extinction" title="Late Ordovician mass extinction">O–S</a></span></div>
</div>
<div style="visibility:hidden"><div class="noresize"><a href="/wiki/File:Extinction_intensity.svg" title="File:Extinction intensity.svg"><img alt="Extinction intensity.svg" data-file-height="324" data-file-width="531" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Extinction_intensity.svg/320px-Extinction_intensity.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Extinction_intensity.svg/480px-Extinction_intensity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Extinction_intensity.svg/640px-Extinction_intensity.svg.png 2x" usemap="#ImageMap_dd6b8fd031a424b3" width="320"/></a><map name="ImageMap_dd6b8fd031a424b3"><area alt="Cambrian" coords="16,0,46,14" href="/wiki/Cambrian" shape="rect" title="Cambrian"/><area alt="Ordovician" coords="47,0,70,14" href="/wiki/Ordovician" shape="rect" title="Ordovician"/><area alt="Silurian" coords="71,0,86,14" href="/wiki/Silurian" shape="rect" title="Silurian"/><area alt="Devonian" coords="87,0,117,14" href="/wiki/Devonian" shape="rect" title="Devonian"/><area alt="Carboniferous" coords="118,0,151,14" href="/wiki/Carboniferous" shape="rect" title="Carboniferous"/><area alt="Permian" coords="151,0,178,14" href="/wiki/Permian" shape="rect" title="Permian"/><area alt="Triassic" coords="178,0,206,14" href="/wiki/Triassic" shape="rect" title="Triassic"/><area alt="Jurassic" coords="207,0,236,14" href="/wiki/Jurassic" shape="rect" title="Jurassic"/><area alt="Cretaceous" coords="237,0,280,14" href="/wiki/Cretaceous" shape="rect" title="Cretaceous"/><area alt="Paleogene" coords="281,0,304,14" href="/wiki/Paleogene" shape="rect" title="Paleogene"/><area alt="Neogene" coords="304,0,316,14" href="/wiki/Neogene" shape="rect" title="Neogene"/></map></div></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">The Permian–Triassic extinction event (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Dying" title="Great Dying">Great Dying</a>) may have been caused by release of <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clathrate" title="Clathrate">clathrates</a>. An estimated 52% of marine <a href="/wiki/Genus" title="Genus">genera</a> became extinct, representing 96% of all marine <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a>.</div>
</div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sea_ice" title="Sea ice">Sea ice</a>, and the cold conditions it sustains, serves to stabilize <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a> deposits on and near the shoreline,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent2008_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-independent2008-77">[77]</a></sup> preventing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clathrate" title="Clathrate">clathrate</a> breaking down and outgassing <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a> into the atmosphere, causing further warming. Melting of this ice may release large quantities of <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a>, a powerful <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a>, into the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere" title="Atmosphere">atmosphere</a>, causing further warming in a strong <a href="/wiki/Positive_feedback" title="Positive feedback">positive feedback</a> cycle and marine genera and species to become extinct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-independent2008_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-independent2008-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_concerns">Other concerns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Arctic_Ocean&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Other concerns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Other <a href="/wiki/Environmentalism" title="Environmentalism">environmental concerns</a> relate to the <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_contamination" title="Radioactive contamination">radioactive contamination</a> of the Arctic Ocean from, for example, Russian <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_waste" title="Radioactive waste">radioactive waste</a> dump sites in the Kara Sea,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_testing" title="Nuclear weapons testing">nuclear test sites</a> such as Novaya Zemlya,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Camp_Century" title="Camp Century">Camp Century</a>'s contaminants in Greenland,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> and radioactive contamination from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fukushima_Daiichi_nuclear_disaster" title="Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster">Fukushima Daiichi nuclear disaster</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 July 2015, five nations (United States, Russia, Canada, Norway, Denmark/Greenland) signed a declaration committing to keep their fishing vessels out of a 1.1 million square mile zone in the central Arctic Ocean near the North Pole. The agreement calls for those nations to refrain from fishing there until there is better scientific knowledge about the marine resources and until a regulatory system is in place to protect those resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
